Cross reference- Dancing in liquor establishments, § 4-45; live shows at liquor establishments, § 4-46; businesses, ch. 12; licensed public events and festivals, § 28-46. 
State Law reference- Shows and exhibits, G.L. 1956, § 5-22-1 et seq.; local licensing of amusements, G.L. 1956, § 5-22-5. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 6-1-6-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OPEN RECREATIONAL EVENTS AND AMUSEMENTS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 6-31-6-50. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 6-51. - Required. 
    It shall be unlawful to conduct or operate a recreational event or amusement within the town which is open to the general public where a fee is charged without having first obtained a license therefor from the town council. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § I) 
Sec. 6-52. - Relief from zoning board of review required prior to acceptance of application. 
    If the proposed event is not a permitted use as of right under the town zoning ordinance (chapter 38), then the applicant must first obtain the necessary relief from the town zoning board of review before his license application shall be accepted. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § II) 
Sec. 6-53. - Application deadline; contents. 
    Written application for the license shall be made to the town council no less than 30 days prior to the date of the scheduled event or the date of the first scheduled event should the license application be for a series of entertainment dates. This application shall include a checklist, to be obtained from the town clerk, and shall specify the name and address of the applicant, the nature of the proposed entertainment, location and dates of proposed entertainments, as well as what provisions will be made for medical assistance, fire protection, police protection, parking facilities, protection of the neighboring property, crowd control and sanitary facilities. Any requirements or demands made by the council shall be borne by the applicant. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § III) 
Sec. 6-54. - Notice to owners of meeting. 
    Upon receipt of such application, the town clerk shall schedule the application to be brought before the town council at a regular council meeting. A notice shall be sent by regular mail at least one week prior to the scheduled meeting to the owners of all properties within 300 feet of the perimeter of the premises in or on which the entertainment is sought to be located. The application and time and location of the meeting should also be advertised in a newspaper of general circulation in the town by the town clerk. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § IV) 
Sec. 6-55. - Notice to chief of police and building inspector of meeting; purpose. 
    The town clerk shall also give similar notice to the chief of police and building inspector at least one week prior to the meeting so that the application and the provisions set forth in section 6-52 can be reviewed. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § V) 
Sec. 6-56. - Fees. 
    Each applicant for a license to operate a recreational event or amusement shall pay the town clerk, upon filing the application, a license fee of $25.00, plus the cost of mail and advertising. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § VI) 
State Law reference- License fee for shows, G.L. 1956, § 5-22-2012. 
Sec. 6-57. - Review of application; approval or approval with conditions. 
    The town council shall review each license application at a regular town council meeting on the date scheduled by the town clerk. The application may be approved by the town council or approved with conditions, which may include, but not be limited to, hours of operation and duration of the event. The town clerk may grant such license only if the town council shall find that the proposed entertainment would not constitute a public nuisance and that the chief of police finds all requirements set forth in section 6-53 have been met. The council shall not consider an application for the issuance of a license before the building inspector and chief of police have reviewed the application as evidenced by their signatures on the application checklist. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § VII) 
Sec. 6-58. - Assignment of police officers after application evaluation. 
    The chief of police shall assign the number of police officers as deemed necessary after evaluating the application. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § VIII) 
Sec. 6-59. - Barriers to issuance. 
    No amusement/event license shall be issued to any applicant currently in arrears in any tax or assessment levied by the town, or for use upon any premises for which any such taxes or assessments are unpaid at the time of the filing of the application. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § IX) 
Sec. 6-60. - Violation of division to result in revocation. 
    Any violation of the provisions of this division or of any other town ordinance shall be grounds for immediate revocation of the license. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § X) 
State Law reference- Revocation of license, G.L. 1956, § 5-22-2012. 
Sec. 6-61. - Waiver of bond, license fee and other division requirements. 
    The town council, at its discretion, may require the posting of a surety bond, waive the license fee and/or waive any of the requirements in this division. 
(Ord. of 10-5-1995(2), § XI) 
Secs. 6-62-6-95. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - AMUSEMENT DEVICES AND GAMEROOMS[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Pinball and game room licensing, G.L. 1956, § 5-2-2010. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 6-96. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Amusement device or game means any mechanical, electric, electronic or video device used or designed to be operated for entertainment or as a game by the insertion of a coin, slug, token, plate or disk or in similar fashion, whether or not registering a score and whether or not its operation demands skill or chance, or both. It shall include, but not be limited to, such devices as marble machines, pinball machines, skillball, mechanical grab or displayed games, air games, video display or computer games, so-called and all games similar thereto under whatever name they may be called. 
    Gameroom means any establishment containing four or more amusement games. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, §§ 2, 3) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 6-97. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating any of the provisions of this article, in addition to the revocation of his license, shall be liable to be punished according to the provisions of section 1-7. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 14) 
Sec. 6-98. - Hours of operation. 
    No gameroom or amusement machines shall be operated on Sunday. No gameroom or amusement devices shall be operated after the hours of 10:00 p.m. or before 12:00 noon. This section shall not apply to establishments which hold a class B tavern license. Such establishments may keep their gamerooms and amusement machines open for operation during the hours which their class B license permits them to be open. No person under the legal drinking age shall operate a machine in any tavern holding a class B license at any time. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 11) 
Sec. 6-99. - Operation of machine by underaged persons. 
    No person holding a license under this article shall permit persons under the age of 16 years to play or operate any amusement device or machine unless such person is accompanied by a parent or guardian. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 9) 
Sec. 6-100. - Gambling devices; seizure and impoundment; destruction. 
    If the chief of police shall have reason to believe that any amusement device is used as a gambling device, such device may be seized by the police and impounded. If, upon trial of the exhibitor for allowing it to be used as a gambling device, such exhibitor is found guilty, such machine shall be destroyed by the police. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 13) 
Sec. 6-101. - Location restrictions. 
    No license shall be issued for any location which is within 1,000 feet from a school building as measured from the closest point of the school building to the main entrance of such building in which the gameroom or amusement machines or devices are located. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 10) 
Sec. 6-102. - Machines presently in operation; new or unlicensed machines. 
    All machines presently in existence and in operation in places of business at the date of adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived will be entitled to a license upon payment of a prorated fee if such fee is paid prior to September 30, 1982. Thereafter, any unlicensed machine or any new machine which seeks to be licensed must receive the approval of the town council after filing an application as required by this article. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 16) 
Secs. 6-103-6-125. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 6-126. - Required. 
    No person shall keep for public patronage any amusement device or game within the town without a license from the town. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 1) 
Sec. 6-127. - Application; fee; issuance of sticker. 
    Application for a license shall be made to the town council upon a form to be supplied by the town clerk. The fee for a license is $50.00 per machine per year commencing on December 1 of each year and expiring on November 30 of each year. The town clerk shall issue a sticker to be attached to the machine on a yearly basis. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 4) 
Sec. 6-128. - Limit on number issued; exception. 
    No more than three licenses shall be issued for any one establishment except that an establishment wishing to operate four or more amusement games must first obtain a variance or special exception from the zoning board of review. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 5) 
Sec. 6-129. - Application fee; hearing; contents of application. 
    An applicant for a license shall, upon filing the application form, pay an application fee of $10.00 and an advertising fee. The town clerk shall forward each new application to the chief of police for his report to the town council, and a public hearing will be held on the application after notice in a local newspaper for three weeks. The application for such license shall contain the following information: 
(1)  Name and address of the applicant, age, date and place of birth. 
(2)  Prior convictions of applicant, if any. 
(3)  Place where the machine or device is to be operated and the business conducted at that place. 
(4)  Description of machine to be covered by the license, name of manufacturer and serial number. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 6) 
Sec. 6-130. - Transfer-From person to person or place to place. 
    A license shall not be transferable from person to person or place to place and shall be usable only at the place and by the person designated on the license. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 7) 
Sec. 6-131. - Same-From one machine or device to another. 
    A license may be transferred from one machine or device to another similar machine upon application to the town clerk to such effect and giving of a description and a serial number of the new machine or device. Not more than one machine shall be operated under one license, and the applicant or licensee shall be required to secure a license for each and every machine displaced or operated by him. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 8) 
Sec. 6-132. - Revocation; hearing. 
    Every license issued under this article is subject to the right, which is hereby expressly reserved, to revoke the license should the licensee, directly or indirectly, permit the operation of any mechanical or electrical amusement device contrary to the provisions of this article or the laws of the state. Such license may be revoked by the town council after written notice of a hearing to the licensee, which notice shall specify the ordinance or law violations with which the licensee is charged and, after a hearing, if the licensee is found to be guilty of such violations. Ten days' notice of this hearing shall be given the licensee. 
(Ord. of 9-9-1982, § 12) 
Chapter 8 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Supplementary zoning regulations pertaining to animals, § 38-290. 
State Law reference- Animals generally, G.L. 1956, § 4-1-1 et seq.; maximum penalty for violation of dog ordinance, G.L. 1956, § 4-13-1; cruelty to animals, G.L. 1956, § 4-1-1 et seq.; poisoning animals, G.L. 1956, § 4-13-2013; power of council to regulate dogs, G.L. 1956, § 4-13-1; town ordinances, contagious diseases, G.L. 1956, § 4-4-2018; municipal regulation of animals, G.L. 1956, § 23-19.2-1; animals at large, G.L. 1956, § 4-15-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 8-1-8-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Officers and employees, § 2-61 et seq. 

Sec. 8-31. - Scope of authority. 
    Since the animal control officer is representing the town, he shall be under the direction of the chief of police. The animal control officer must be aware that he does not act for himself but for the public and for the good name and reputation of the town police department and the town. 
(Ord. of 7-23-1981) 
Sec. 8-32. - Supervision. 
    The animal control officer shall be under the supervision of the chief of police who will have the overall supervision of the animal control officer and shall be responsible for the enforcement of all laws, ordinances and regulations which the animal control officer has authority to execute. 
(Ord. of 7-23-1981, § I) 
Sec. 8-33. - Qualifications. 
    The animal control officer must have the following qualifications: 
(1)  An American citizen in good physical condition. 
(2)  A person of good reputation in the community and free from intemperate or immoral habits. He shall not have been convicted of a felony, misdemeanor or habitually consorted with criminals, persons of ill repute or have been engaged in or connected with any illegal or illicit business. 
(3)  Some experience in the keeping and care of animals of various types and breeds, especially dogs, and a respect and liking for dogs and other animals. 
(4)  The ability to maintain courteous relations with all sectors of the public. 
(5)  A graduate from a standard high school or its equivalent or any equivalent combination and experience. 
(6)  In possession of a valid state driver's license. 
(7)  A special constable in the town. 
(Ord. of 7-23-1981, § II) 
Sec. 8-34. - Duties. 
    The duties of the animal control officer are as follows: 
(1)  Ascertain and make a list of the owners or keepers of dogs. 
(2)  Report and be present for duty no more than 20 hours per week. 
(3)  Be neat and clean about his person and shall keep his body clean as circumstances will permit. 
(4)  Comply with the instructions from the police dispatcher. Messages and communications transmitted will be obeyed and communication transmitted by the dispatcher shall not be refused unless so directed by a superior officer. 
(5)  Investigate and answer all complaints received during working hours or as received and settle complaints tactfully. 
(6)  Investigate and answer all complaints that require followup investigations, regardless of the date and time reported. 
(7)  Pick up all dead animals or strays, including dogs, cats and other small animals. 
(8)  Dispose of all dead animals in a safe and sanitary way. 
(9)  Gather injured or strayed animals such as cats, dogs and other domestic pets upon a complaint to do so. 
(10)  Impound strays and contact owners upon determination and return or release animals to the rightful owners. 
(11)  Clean and disinfect the animal control vehicle. 
(12)  Enforce the laws of the state and town ordinances pertaining to animals. 
(13)  Impound animals upon complaint for the duration of appropriate tests and incubation period for such diseases as rabies. 
(14)  Work in close cooperation with various agencies such as the Animal Rescue League and the Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Animals. 
(15)  Keep, or cause to be kept, accurate and detailed records of the impoundment and the disposition of all animals taken into custody. 
(16)  Keep, or cause to be kept, accurate and detailed records of all bite cases and shall have a police officer respond to all cases involving bites so that a police case report may be made. 
(17)  Keep, or cause to be kept, accurate and detailed records of all monies belonging to the town. 
(Ord. of 7-23-1981, § III) 
Sec. 8-35. - Operation of motor vehicle. 
(a)  No one shall operate the animal control vehicle without a valid license to operate such vehicle. 
(b)  No one shall operate the animal control vehicle without authority. 
(c)  No person shall be permitted to ride as a passenger in the animal control vehicle unless necessary for the proper performance of duty. 
(d)  The animal control officer shall maintain a written daily vehicle report indicating mileage, gasoline usage and vehicle condition. 
(e)  When leaving the animal control vehicle unattended, the officer shall lock the ignition, remove the keys and lock the doors. 
(f)  While operating the animal control vehicle, the animal control officer shall be in radio communication with the dispatcher. 
(Ord. of 7-23-1981, § IV) 
Cross reference- Traffic, ch. 36. 
Sec. 8-36. - Discipline. 
(a)  The chief of police has the authority to punish any animal control officer for failure to obey the regulations as set forth in this article as well as all general and special orders and orders of superior officers. 
(b)  The offenses for which the animal control officer is subject to punishment are as follows: 
(1)  Commission of a crime or misdemeanor under any statute or ordinance; 
(2)  Disobedience or violation of any department regulation, rules, order, instruction or memorandum; 
(3)  Insubordination; 
(4)  Neglect of duty; 
(5)  Gross inefficiency; 
(6)  Gross incompetence; 
(7)  Unnecessary violence or indignity to a citizen; 
(8)  Absence from duty; 
(9)  Negligence in the care of public property, its abuse, misuse, waste or willful destruction; 
(10)  False official statement, oral or written; 
(11)  Communicating information relating to police business to unauthorized persons; or 
(12)  Intoxication. 
(Ord. of 7-23-1981, § V) 
Secs. 8-37-8-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DOGS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 8-71. - Foster Old Home Days, dogs restricted. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person or owner to permit or cause any dog, whether licensed or leashed, to be on or along the grounds and location designated for any Foster Old Home Days during any time which is designated for said event. However, this section shall not apply to Seeing Eye Dogs assisting the blind or handicap persons, or such other personal service dogs or animals that are controlled by such persons and/or their companions. 
(Ord. of 5-25-2017) 
Editor's note- An ordinance May 25, 2017, set out provisions intended for use as § 8-100. For purposes of classification, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as § 8-71. 
Secs. 8-72-8-100. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - IMPOUNDMENT[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to impound, G.L. 1956, § 4-13-2015.1. 

Sec. 8-101. - Authority to impound unlicensed or uncollared dogs. 
    The animal control officer of the town is empowered to impound any dog over the age of one year, running free within the town, which is unlicensed and/or uncollared. 
Sec. 8-102. - Redemption; fees and fines. 
    Any dog so impounded may be redeemed from the pound by its owner or keeper or agent thereof, on payment to the animal control officer of the appropriate fees and fines as per the following schedule: 
(1)  For maintaining an unlicensed and/or uncollared dog ..... $25.00 
License must be in place within 14 calendar days of the issuance of a citation. 
(2)  License fee, annually ..... 7.00 
(3)  Canine surcharge, per G.L. 1956, § 4-24-9 ..... 1.00 
(4)  License late fee ..... 5.00 
(5)  Pound fee, per day ..... 2.00, or such amount as may otherwise be determined by the pound 
    Notwithstanding the foregoing, the license fee set forth in subsection (2) above may be increased by the town clerk to an amount, not to exceed $15.00, if in the town clerk's reasonable discretion the licensing fee is insufficient to cover the cost of administering the licensing of dogs in the town. 
(Ord. of 7-11-2013, § 1) 
Sec. 8-103. - Classification and disposition of unclaimed dogs. 
    All dogs so impounded which remain unclaimed for a period of five days shall, after such confinement, be considered strays and be destroyed. 
Secs. 8-104-8-125. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - LICENSING 

Sec. 8-126. - Required; failure to license; fees. 
    Any owner or keeper of a dog required to be licensed under the provisions of this division, or appropriate state legislation, who fails to license such dog as provided by appropriate legislation (per G.L. 1956 § 4-13-4) shall, after the last business day of April, be assessed a late fee in addition to the license fee, as indicated in section 8-102. 
(Ord. of 3-10-1977, § I; Ord. of 5-5-1977, § 1; Ord. of 4-9-1981, § 1; Ord. of 7-11-2013, § 2) 
Sec. 8-127. - Animal control officer; duties and authority. 
    The town council shall, each year during the month of April, appoint an animal control officer who shall have the following duties and authority: 
(1)  During the month of May, to canvass the town to determine an accurate census of the number of dogs maintained within the town. 
(2)  To issue dog licenses as appropriate and collect such license and late fees as may be due. 
(3)  To report to the town council any and all dogs required to be licensed which remain unlicensed as of May 31. 
(Ord. of 3-10-1977, § II) 
Sec. 8-128. - Disposition of collected fees. 
    The animal control officer shall turn over all fees collected to the town clerk and shall be compensated by the town council in the amount of $5.00 for each license issued by him. 
(Ord. of 3-10-1977, § III) 
Secs. 8-129-8-150. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - RABIES CONTROL[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- Rabies control, G.L. 1956, § 4-13-2029 et seq. 

Sec. 8-151. - Reporting bites; quarantine; examination. 
    Every dog which bites a person shall be promptly reported to the animal control officer, and shall thereupon be securely quarantined at the direction of the animal control officer for a period of 14 days. Upon demand of the animal control officer, the owner or keeper of such dog shall, at his own expense, cause such dog to be examined for rabies by a licensed veterinarian who shall furnish a written report of his examination to the animal control officer. In cases where such examination has been demanded, the dog shall remain quarantined until the animal control officer has received the veterinarian's report. 
Sec. 8-152. - Confinement of biting dogs. 
    In addition to the quarantine and examination set forth in section 8-151, every dog which bites a person while off the premises of its owner or keeper shall thereafter be kept confined on the premises of its owner or keeper or in a kennel (except that it shall be allowed to leave such premises or kennel confined in a motor vehicle or under control on a leash). 
Sec. 8-153. - Habitual biting or attacking dogs. 
    Every dog which habitually bites or attacks other dogs or domestic animals while off the premises of its owner or keeper shall, at the direction of the animal control officer, be kept confined as provided in section 8-152. 
Sec. 8-154. - Unspayed female dogs; period of confinement. 
    The animal control officer may from time to time direct the owner or keeper of any unspayed female dog to keep such dog confined as provided in section 8-152. Such period of confinement shall not exceed 21 days at any one time. 
Sec. 8-155. - Failure to obey animal control officer's orders; seizure of animal; payment of fees; disposition of dog on failure to claim. 
    If the owner or keeper of any dog shall fail to obey an order of the animal control officer as to quarantine, confinement or veterinarian examination, the animal control officer is empowered to seize such dog and may enter upon the premises of the owner or keeper to do so. Thereafter, the owner or keeper shall be liable to the town for the cost of picking up such dog, $5.00, for the cost of impoundment $2.00 per day, and for the expense of examination by a veterinarian. The animal control officer shall not be obliged to surrender such dog to the owner or keeper until all such fees and expenses are paid in full. If after five days the owner or keeper does not reclaim such dog and pay the fees and expenses, the animal control officer is empowered and authorized to kill the dog and charge the expense of execution and disposal, $5.00, to the owner or keeper. 
Sec. 8-156. - Seizure of nuisance dog; notice to owner; payment of fees; disposal on failure of owner to claim. 
    The animal control officer is authorized to seize any dog which is causing a nuisance while off the premises of its owner. After seizing such dog the animal control officer shall notify the owner or keeper of such dog, if such owner or keeper is known to the animal control officer, and the animal control officer shall surrender such dog to its owner or keeper upon payment to the town of $5.00 for the cost of picking up the dog and $2.00 per day for the cost of impoundment. If five days after being notified the owner or keeper does not reclaim the dog and pay the fees and expenses, the animal control officer is empowered and authorized to kill the dog and charge the expense of execution and disposal for the dog and charge the expense of execution and disposal, $5.00, to the owner or keeper. 
Sec. 8-157. - Penalty for violation of division. 
    Any person violating this division shall be punished according to the provisions of section 1-7. 
Secs. 8-158-8-190. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - KENNELS[5] 
Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 12. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 8-191. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be fined not exceeding $5.00 for each day such kennel is so kept. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § X) 
Secs. 8-192-8-215. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSES[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 8-216. - Classes. 
    Kennel licenses shall be issued by the town in two classes: 
(1)  Class A. A class A license shall be issued to keepers of thoroughbred dogs kept for breeding purposes and for sale either on the premises or other commercial outlet. Note: The raising of animals for sale is permitted in AR and MI districts only and prohibited in NC and HC districts. (See section 38-191 et seq.) 
(2)  Class B. Class B licenses shall be issued to keepers of dogs kept for boarding purposes only. Kennel licenses shall be issued only to keepers or owners of dogs to be housed on the same parcel of land where the owner or keeper resides. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § I) 
Sec. 8-217. - Application for initial issuance. 
    Every owner or keeper of dogs qualified to apply for a kennel license shall file with the town clerk an application for the initial issuance of a kennel license. Such application shall be filed at least two weeks prior to the date requested for a hearing. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § II) 
Sec. 8-218. - Contents of application. 
    Such application shall state the name of the owner and/or keeper of such kennel, the address of such owner and/or keeper, the proposed location of such kennel, the name and address of the owner of the land of such proposed location, the number of dogs to be kept at such kennel and that the dogs are to be kept for breeding and stud purposes only or for boarding purposes, the names of all adjoining owners and all property owners within 500 feet of such proposed location, the number of dogs to be kept at such kennel and that the dogs are to be kept for breeding and stud purposes only or for boarding purposes. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § III) 
Sec. 8-219. - Notice of hearing. 
    Upon receipt of such application, the town clerk shall cause notice of such application for the initial issuance of a kennel license to be published in the Providence Journal or Evening Bulletin at least once during the week prior to the week in which the hearing will be held. Notice shall also be given by the town clerk by registered or certified mail to all owners of adjoining property and all property owners within 500 feet of the proposed location, to be mailed at least one week prior to the hearing on the application. Such notice shall state the name and address of the applicant, the type of license requested and the location for which the license is requested. Such notice shall also state that all persons are entitled to be heard before the granting of such license and shall state the time and place of hearing. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § IV) 
Sec. 8-220. - Hearing. 
    Hearings on applications for the initial issuance of kennel licenses shall be held at regularly scheduled town council meetings unless otherwise ordered by the town council. At such hearing, all persons for or against the granting of such license shall be heard. Hearings shall be open to the public. The town council shall make its decision and grant or deny such license within ten days after the date of hearing. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § V) 
Sec. 8-221. - Fees. 
    Each applicant for the initial issuance of a kennel license shall pay to the town clerk, upon filing his application, a license fee of $25.00 for such license. Each applicant for the initial issuance of a kennel license shall also pay upon filing the sum of $25.00 to defray the costs of giving notice and conducting the hearing. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § VI) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, G.L. 1956, § 4-13-2011. 
Sec. 8-222. - Renewal. 
    Application for the renewal of a kennel license shall be made to the town clerk on or before April 1 in each year. Such application shall contain the same information as the application for the initial issuance of a kennel license as set forth in section 8-218. Upon receipt of a proper and timely application, and upon the payment of a license fee of $25.00, if the number of dogs to be kept does not exceed ten and a license fee of $25.00 if the number of dogs to be kept exceeds ten, the town clerk shall issue a renewal of the kennel license to the applicant. All fees so collected by the town clerk shall be paid over by him to the town treasurer. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § VII) 
Sec. 8-223. - Expiration. 
    All kennel licenses shall expire on April 1 in each year. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § VIII) 
Sec. 8-224. - Revocation. 
    Kennel licenses may be revoked by the town council if the kennel and the use and operation thereof at its location constitutes a public nuisance or if the license is in violation of any of the provisions of this article. Notice of proposed revocation shall be given to the licensee by registered or certified mail addressed to the licensee at the address contained in the application for a kennel license and deposited in the mail at least two weeks prior to the date set for hearing. The town council may also give such further notice as it may deem necessary. Hearings shall be open to the public and all interested persons shall be heard. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § IX) 
Sec. 8-225. - Exceptions. 
    The provisions of this article shall not apply to the operation or maintenance of a pet shop as defined by state law, nor to any boarding or keeping of dogs in conjunction with medical treatment by a licensed veterinarian. 
(Ord. of 11-1-1968, § XII) 
Chapter 10 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Manufactured homes and trailers, ch. 16; nuisances, ch. 18; planning, ch. 24; soil erosion and sediment control, ch. 26; solid waste management, ch. 28; streets and sidewalks, ch. 30; subdivision regulations, ch. 32; zoning, ch. 38. 
State Law reference- State Building Code, G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-100.0 et seq.; inspection of buildings where combustible materials accumulate, G.L. 1956, § 23-28.5-1 et seq.; notice to vacate unfit dwellings, G.L. 1956, § 23-19.2-8; housing maintenance and occupancy code, G.L. 1956, § 45-24.3-1 et seq.; minimum housing standards, G.L. 1956, § 45-24.2-1 et seq.; plumbers, G.L. 1956, § 5-20-1 et seq.; electricians, G.L. 1956, § 5-6-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 10-1. - Enforcement; penalty for violation of chapter. 
(a)  Any person having any duty to perform under the provisions of this chapter may, so far as may be necessary for the performance of his duties, enter any building or premises in the town without being guilty of trespass; provided, however, that the building inspector shall not enter any occupied dwelling without the permission of the owner. Unreasonable refusal of such permission shall be grounds for revocation of a permit. 
(b)  Any person violating any provision of this chapter wherein no penalty is otherwise prescribed in this article shall be fined in an amount up to $100.00 for every violation thereof, and each day of the existence of any such violation shall be deemed a separate offense. Such fines shall inure to the town. 
(c)  The town may cause suit to be brought in the supreme or superior court in the name of the town to restrain the violation of and compel compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(d)  Applications for variance under the provision of the state building code shall be made to the town zoning board of review and shall follow the same procedures as other applications to the review board. 
Sec. 10-2. - Building inspector; appointment and duties. 
(a)  The town council shall appoint a building inspector who shall serve at the pleasure of the town council and until his successor is appointed. Appointments to the office of building inspector shall be based on such qualifications for education and experience as set by the town council necessary for the proper performance of the office. 
(b)  It shall be the duty of the building inspector to issue and revoke building permits and to enforce the provisions of this chapter and any subsequent amendments adopted by the town council. The building inspector shall examine all structures during the course of their erection, alteration, repair, moving or demolition to ensure compliance with the provisions of this chapter and other applicable ordinances of the town, and shall record all violations which shall be reported to the town council and to the town solicitor. 
(c)  The building inspector shall make a written monthly report to the town council at each regular meeting concerning the number of applicants received, permits issued or refused and fees received. 
Cross reference- Officers and employees, § 2-61 et seq. 
State Law reference- Local building inspector, G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-107.1.1. 
Secs. 10-3-10-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BUILDING CODE 

Sec. 10-36. - Conformance of all construction and alteration to state building code. 
    All construction and alteration, subject to the provisions of this chapter and requiring the issuance of a building permit, shall conform to the applicable construction requirements as set forth in the state building code. 
State Law reference- State Building Code to apply throughout state, G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-100.1.7. 
Sec. 10-37. - Subdivision, zoning and other regulations. 
    Any structure erected, repaired, altered, moved or demolished under the provisions of this chapter shall conform to the town subdivision ordinance, the town zoning ordinance, and to other applicable ordinances of the town. 
Cross reference- Subdivision regulations, ch. 32; zoning, ch. 38. 
Sec. 10-38. - Board of review. 
(a)  The town zoning board of review shall constitute the board of appeal from the inspector of buildings in the town. 
(b)  Appeals to the board of review may be taken by any party aggrieved or by any officer, department of board affected by any order or decision of the building inspector concerning the provisions of this chapter. Such appeal shall be taken within a reasonable time as provided in the rules of the board of review by filing with the building inspector and with the board of review a notice of appeal specifying the grounds for appeal. In no case shall this reasonable time exceed 30 days. 
(c)  The board of review shall fix a reasonable time for the hearing of an appeal and shall publish notice of the hearing at least one week prior to the date of such hearing in a newspaper of general circulation in the town; shall give due notice to the applicant, abutting owners and other parties in interest; and shall hear and decide the appeal within a reasonable time. Any party may appear at the hearing in person, by agent or by attorney. An appeal shall be heard within 40 days from the date of filing, and the decision thereon shall be filed within 15 days after the completion of the hearing. 
(d)  Each appeal shall be accompanied by a fee in the amount of $100.00 payable to the town. 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2. 
State Law reference- Local boards of review, G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-127.2. 
Sec. 10-39. - Special regulations. 
(a)  Excavations. Where an excavation lies within five feet of the line of a public right-of-way, it shall be enclosed within a barricade at least three feet in height and shall be suitably lighted during the hours between sunset and sunrise. 
(b)  Public right-of-way. No person shall store building materials, machinery or construction vehicles within a public right-of-way without the prior written approval of the building inspector and the public works director. 
(c)  Rubbish. Within ten days after completion or demolition of a building or work upon a building, or at such time (after the ten-day period) as may be required by the building inspector, all rubbish and other discarded material shall be removed from the premises by the applicant or his agent. Failure to do so will subject the applicant to a charge of violation of this chapter. 
(d)  Moving a building. Any person wishing to move a building or structure to a new location must obtain a building permit. No electric wire, telephone wire, sign, tree or shrub shall be removed in connection with such moving without the written permission of the building inspector. Any person who intends to move a building or structure into the town must obtain a building permit. All such buildings or structures shall conform to the applicable provisions of the state building code. Any person moving a structure or building must file with the permit application a bond or other surety satisfactory to the town solicitor, and conditioned to comply with all legal requirements and restrictions relative to the moving of buildings; and to pay damages suffered by any person by reason of any negligence of the licensee, his servants or agents in or about the moving of buildings in the town; and to indemnify and save the town harmless from all loss and damage by reason of any such negligence in moving buildings through, over or on any public street or highway in the town; and any liability of the town therefore relative to maintaining its public highways in condition safe and convenient for pedestrian and vehicular travel of any description. Such permit may be revoked at any time by the building inspector for any violation of this chapter or any of the conditions of the bond. 
State Law reference- Moving, raising, shoring or demolition of buildings, G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-116.0. et seq. 
(e)  Plumbing. All drainage fixtures, gas fixtures and piping shall conform to the requirements as specified in appropriate sections of the state building code. 
(f)  Electrical. All electrical wiring and installation shall conform to the latest edition of the National Electrical Code published by the National Fire Protection Association, 60 Battery March Street, Boston, Massachusetts 02110. 
Secs. 10-40-10-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - BUILDING PERMITS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Building permit required, G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-113.1. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 10-71. - Required; application; fees. 
    Any person, group of persons or corporation contemplating the erection, extension, alteration or repairs, moving or demolition of a structure, or contemplating the structural alteration, electrical wiring or installation of plumbing in an existing structure which work shall cost or have a value of over $500.00, shall make application for a permit on the prescribed forms in the office of the building inspector. One copy of the approved applications shall be retained by the building inspector, and one copy shall be filed with the tax assessor. Such application shall be submitted at least ten days prior to the start of construction, except that in the case of an emergency, the building inspector may waive the ten-day period, and shall be accompanied by a fee payable to the building inspector, to be used as part of his remuneration according to the following schedule: 
(1)  Valuation rates; new construction. New construction valuation rates are as follows: 
a.  Main floor, per square foot ..... $60.00 
b.  Second floor, per square foot ..... 40.00 
c.  Walkout breezeway or finish basement, per square foot ..... 30.00 
d.  Garage, attached under, per square foot ..... 25.00 
e.  Garage, unattached, per square foot ..... 30.00 
f.  Barn, per square foot ..... 30.00 
g.  Addition to house, family room, etc., per square foot ..... 30.00 
h.  Addition to house, kitchen or bath, per square foot ..... 40.00 
i.  Pole barn, per square foot ..... 15.00 
j.  Deck, per square foot ..... 10.00 
k.  Porch, per square foot ..... 12.00 
l.  Dormer, per square foot ..... 20.00 
(2)  Average house. Permit fees for an average house are as follows: 
a.  Plumbing estimate $3,000.00 ..... $35.00 
(Over 11/2 baths or jacuzzi) ..... 50.00 
b.  Mechanical estimate $3,000.00 ..... 35.00 
c.  Wood stove ..... 15.00 
d.  Electrical estimate $3,000.00 ..... 35.00 
Electric heat ..... 50.00 
Temporary service ..... 15.00 
Pool wiring ..... 35.00 
(3)  Fee adjustment for extensive work. Fees shall be adjusted at $5.00 per thousand dollars of valuation for extensive work. 
(4)  Demolition. The demolition fee shall be $15.00. 
(5)  Size requirement. A permit is required for any structure over eight feet by eight feet. 
(6)  Building fee valuation. Building fee valuation shall be as follows: 
a.  $1.00-$1,000.00 ..... $ 25.00 
b.  $1,000.00-$10,000.00 ..... 25.00 
Plus per 1,000 valuation ..... 5.00 
c.  $10,000.00 and above ..... 100.00 
Plus per 1,000 valuation ..... 2.50 
(7)  Late filing fee. Late filing fees are as follows: 
a.  First offense: Double the standard fee and/or $200.00 fine. 
b.  Second offense: Triple the standard fee and/or $500.00 fine. 
State Law reference- Municipalities to prescribe building permit fees, G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-118.0. 
Sec. 10-72. - Required prior to construction. 
    No construction work other than preliminary grading shall be done without the issuance of a valid building permit. 
Sec. 10-73. - Validity upon identification of construction site on town's plat maps. 
    No building permit shall be valid unless the location of such permitted construction is properly identified by reference to the tax assessor's plat maps of the town. 
Sec. 10-74. - Additional maps and plans prior to issuance; construction start deadline following issuance. 
    The building inspector may require any additional information, maps and plans that he deems necessary in issuing a permit. Construction must be commenced within one year after the date of issuance of a building permit, and the permit shall not be valid if construction is not commenced within such period. 
Sec. 10-75. - Renewal of expired permit; transfer. 
    Permits that have expired without any act of construction may be renewed upon application to the building inspector, and the fee may be waived upon such renewal in the discretion of the building board of review. A building permit shall not be transferable. 
Sec. 10-76. - Denial or revocation. 
    Any act of construction not in conformity with this article and any false representation in any statement submitted in the application for building permit shall be cause for the denial or revocation of a building permit. The denial or revocation of a building permit shall be made by the building inspector to the applicant, in writing, precisely stating the reasons for such action by registered or certified mail to the applicant. 
Sec. 10-77. - Site review for commercial construction required prior to issuance; scope of review. 
    No building permit shall be issued for any commercial building or other commercial construction in any zone of the town until a site review of the proposed construction has first been conducted by the planning board. Such review shall cover: 
(1)  Safe highway access to and from the property; 
(2)  Disposal of wastes on the site; 
(3)  Toxic or hazardous materials to be stored or used on the site; 
(4)  Lighting on the site; 
(5)  Effect of the development on the ecology of the site and neighboring properties, with a particular view to the protection of wetlands and rare and unusual plants in the vicinity; 
(6)  Unusual site conditions such as steep slopes, rock formations, springs and the like; and 
(7)  Historical or archaeological features at the site. 
Secs. 10-78-10-100. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - GROWTH MANAGEMENT ISSUANCE RESTRICTIONS 

Sec. 10-101. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this division is to fairly distribute permits for residential development among applicants over time, and to guide the form of development so as to minimize the burden on facilities, primarily schools, and other resources that are at capacity. It is the intent of these provisions to provide for the housing needs of all population groups in a manner which is consistent with the Rhode Island Comprehensive Planning and Land Use Regulation Act (G.L. 1956, § 45-22.2-1 et seq.), with the Foster Comprehensive Community Plan and with Land Use 2010: State Land Use Policies and Plan. 
Sec. 10-102. - Findings. 
    The town council, planning board, town staff and consultants have conducted studies and have followed state planning documents in order to develop a growth management program as called for in the comprehensive community plan. The town council finds that these studies and documents, listed below, establish the basis for the town's growth management plan, and are incorporated herein by reference: 
(1)  Foster Growth Management Program, Andrew Teitz, Esq., and Samuel Shamoon, February 2004. 
(2)  Conceptual Design Options: Building Feasibility Study for Foster/Glocester Regional School, Aharonian and Associates, Inc., August 5, 2003. 
(3)  Town of Foster Comprehensive Plan - 2003 Update, February 2004. 
(4)  Capital Improvement Budgets, Town of Foster, RI, as adopted annually by the town council for fiscal years 1958 through present. 
Sec. 10-103. - Basic residential requirements. 
(a)  Issuance of building permits authorizing creation of one or more additional dwelling units through new construction or change of use shall be allowed only under the procedures and requirements set forth herein. 
(b)  Applicants for such residential building permits shall be authorized in accordance with the priority assigned to them in section 10-108. Applicants shall be assigned dates to begin construction by the building official so that the total number of dwelling units authorized to begin construction in any quarter does not exceed either the 12-month quota as established in section 10-104. The term "quarter" shall mean a period of three consecutive calendar months, beginning on the first day of the first month and continuing through three consecutive months. 
Sec. 10-104. - 12-month quota. 
(a)  Definitions. The term "12-month quota" shall mean the maximum number of residential dwelling units that may be authorized by building permits, except for exemptions as provided herein, during any continuous 12-month period, beginning on July 1 and ending on June 30. 
(b)  Established. The 12-month quota shall be established as follows: 
(1)  On or before the end of the second quarter (December 31, 2004), the planning and building departments shall issue a written report detailing the issuance of permits, exemptions and an analysis of the following data: 
a.  The town's ability to provide public local school capacity over the period of the current capital improvement budget. 
b.  The town's ability to provide regional school capacity over the period of the current capital improvement budget. 
c.  The demands upon capacity that are anticipated to be made by nonresidential development and by residential development not subject to the development priority provisions or exempted in previous years but not yet constructed. 
(2)  The town council has determined, based upon studies conducted pursuant to the comprehensive plan, that the town's present six-year capacity for additional dwelling units within its sustainable and serviceable limits equals not more than 156 dwelling units in addition to those now existing. 
(3)  Any application for a building permit creating one or more additional dwelling units submitted after the effective date of this article shall be subject to the review procedures set forth in section 10-106. Permit applications submitted before the effective date of the ordinance from which this division is derived shall not be subject to any of the quota limitations of this division. 
(4)  The town council shall set the town's six-year capacity as part of its annual capital improvement budget approval without necessity of amending the provisions of the zoning ordinance. During the capital improvement budget approval, an assessment will be provided by the planning department to the town council members detailing the local and regional school capacity and the current annual enrollment at said schools. For purposes of administering this division, the council's determination of the town's six-year capacity shall take effect upon its adoption. 
Sec. 10-105. - Dwelling units exempt from the quota. 
    The following types of dwellings shall not be subject to the provisions of this division with regard to the 12-month or current quarterly quota. These types of dwellings have been determined to have no or minimal impact upon the town's capacity for additional dwelling units within its sustainable and serviceable limits or they provide positive benefits to the town that are consistent with the comprehensive community plan. The building official shall accept applications for construction of the types of dwelling units listed below and shall act upon them without regard to the quotas, priority determination and procedures as set forth in this article. All such permits issued shall be considered to be issued in addition to the 12-month or quarterly quota provisions of this division. 
(1)  Protected development. The application to construct a dwelling unit is not subject to this division because of the vested rights provisions of G.S. 1956, § 45-24-44. 
(2)  Elderly housing. Dwelling units which would contribute to meeting the yearround housing needs of elderly citizens through publicly enforceable restrictions limiting occupancy for a period of not less than 30 years to households at least half or more of whose members are 62 years of age or older. 
(3)  Accessory apartments. Apartment houses are subject to further limitations in the zoning ordinance(chapter 38). 
Sec. 10-106. - Procedure for issuance of building permits. 
(a)  Applications for building permits for construction of one or more dwelling units shall be submitted to the building official, who shall adhere to the following procedure in reviewing and issuing permits: 
(1)  Completeness. The building official shall, upon receipt of an application submitted, examine the application, plans and all materials for completeness, which shall include all plans and materials required for a building permit under the applicable provisions of the zoning ordinance and the state building code. If said application, plans and materials are complete, the building official shall stamp it indicating the date and time of official receipt by the town. 
(2)  Incomplete application. If the application is incomplete and does not contain all plans and materials as required by the zoning ordinance (chapter 38) and the state building code, the application, plans and materials shall be returned to the applicant, within 15 days, who will be informed by the building official what is missing from the submission in order to qualify as a complete application. 
(b)  The building official shall not issue permits for any dwelling units in excess of the quota unless such units are exempt, as provided in section 10-105. The building official shall keep track of all permits issued plus complete applications submitted during the most recent quarter. If, within any quarter, the number exceeds the quota, additional building permits shall no longer be issued. Applications for additional permits shall be accumulated for action at the beginning of the next quarter, and shall be prioritized and issued under the ensuing quarter. 
(c)  At the beginning of the next quarter, the building official shall issue building permits for the accumulated permits held over from the prior quarter. If the quarterly quota has not been met, building permits will be issued for complete applications received during the current quota as provided in this division. 
(d)  The annual number of permits are assigned as follows: 
First quarter July 1 to September 30 seven permits Second quarter October 1 to December 31 six permits Third quarter January 1 to March 31 six permits Fourth quarter April 1 to June 30 seven permits  
Under no circumstances shall the number of building permits, other than those exempt dwellings, exceed the annual quota. 
(e)  In the event that the number of building permits issued in any one year, July 1 to June 30, does not reach the annual quota, there shall be no carryover of permits to the following year. 
Sec. 10-107. - Low or moderate income housing. 
    Dwellings which are authorized under the provisions of the Low and Moderate Income Housing Act (G.L. 1956, § 45-53-1 et seq.) shall be treated as follows: 
(1)  Complete applications for construction of dwelling units so authorized shall be granted permits within the time limits prescribed in the state building code, regardless of the availability of permits within the current quarterly quota, but may be subject to the procedural requirements of section 10-106, or the priority criteria of section 10-108 and the limitations of section 10-109 depending on the procedure of the application; 
(2)  All permits so issued shall be considered to be issued as part of the quota provisions of this article and shall be counted when determining the number of permits issued within the 12-month quota. 
Sec. 10-108. - Priority criteria. 
(a)  Building permits shall be issued by the building official up to the maximum number permitted by the applicable current quarterly quota, in the order of priority assigned below and in accordance with the procedure set forth in section 10-106 and the limitations set forth in section 10-109. In the event of a tie, priority shall go to the application with the earlier date and time of the submission of a complete application. 
(b)  The order of priority shall be as follows: 
(1)  Applicants for development meeting the criteria for low and moderate income housing as defined in G.L. 1956, § 45-53-3(5). 
(2)  Other applicants whose application for construction of a dwelling has been denied for two consecutive quarters because of the provisions of this division, provided that no more than one permit shall be issued to an applicant in this priority until all such available permits for the quarter have been exhausted. 
(3)  Applications for construction of a single household detached dwelling as an individual applicant provided that the property has not been subdivided and a permit has not been granted for other parcels within the subdivided land. 
(4)  Any remaining applications in the order of complete applications received. 
Sec. 10-109. - Limitation on number of authorized units. 
    In order to ensure that residential building permits are equitably distributed among all qualified applicants, the following shall apply: 
(1)  No single applicant shall be granted building permits for more than one dwelling unit during any quarter if doing so would result in denial of a permit for any other applicant. 
(2)  Permits for construction granted priority under the provisions of section 10-108(b)(1), low or moderate income housing, shall be limited to a total of three dwelling units per quarter on a townwide basis if the issuance of more permits would result in denial of a permit for any other applicant for other types of dwellings. If the building official receives applications for more than four such affordable dwelling units in any quarter, priority shall go to the application with the earlier date and time of submittal of a complete application. 
(3)  Notwithstanding the provisions of this division or the provisions of G.S. 1956, § 23-27.3-114.2, nothing herein shall prevent any applicant from accumulating building permits (or commitments for future building permits) over a period of time and using all permits (or commitments) so accumulated to construct a multi-household structure or land development project as a single construction project. 
Sec. 10-110. - Nondwelling development. 
(a)  In acting upon special use permits or variances for developments other than those comprised only of dwelling units, the zoning board of review shall take into consideration the intent of this division, and in acting upon applications for major land development projects, other than those comprised only of dwelling units, the planning board shall do the same. Those boards may require applicants for such special use permits, variances or major land development projects to document the townwide impacts of their proposals upon the following, using a format and materials to be provided by the planning department to facilitate that task: 
(1)  Amount of land resources remaining for development; 
(2)  Impact upon the adequacy of the town's road system; 
(3)  Impact upon public schools; 
(4)  Impact upon the adequacy of public facilities, including town hall, police and fire facilities, library, and recreation facilities. 
(b)  In granting approvals for such permits, each of those boards shall impose such conditions as are appropriate to ensure that the timing of the resulting development will be consistent with the objective to deplete not more than one-third of the town's capacity for additional development within sustainable and serviceable limits in any two years, taking into consideration the documented impacts, the context of impacts from other development, and the mitigation, if any, which has been proposed or required. 
(c)  The provisions of this division shall apply only to applications for development which requires the granting of special use permits other than for a special impact development and/or variances and shall not apply to any use permitted by right in the zoning ordinance (chapter 38). Similarly, major land development projects, if allowed by right in the zoning ordinance (chapter 38), if no special use permits or use variances are required, shall not be subject to the provisions of this division. All such permitted nondwelling uses shall be exempt from the procedural and quota provisions of this division. 
Sec. 10-111. - Expiration of division. 
    This division shall expire December 31, 2010, unless it is earlier extended through amendment of this provision. Upon its expiration, any timing limitations previously placed on building permit availability shall no longer be enforced, but any housing cost or income eligibility stipulations upon which permits were earlier qualified shall remain in full force and effect. 
Sec. 10-112. - Protection against zoning change. 
    Any protection against zoning change provided by this division or by state law (G.L. 1956, § 45-24-44) shall be extended three months each quarter that a building permit application for the dwelling unit in question has been denied. 
Sec. 10-113. - Appeals. 
    Any decision by the building official to carry out the purposes of this division may be appealed by an aggrieved party to the zoning board of review. The appeal shall be taken within 20 days following an action by the building official to enforce the provisions of this division and shall specify the grounds for such appeal. The building official shall forthwith transmit to the zoning board of review all the papers constituting the record upon which the action appealed from was taken. Notice of the appeal shall also be transmitted to the planning board. The procedure for any appeal including a public hearing shall be in accordance with the zoning ordinance (chapter 38).
