ARTICLE II. - LICENSES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Liquor license regulations, § 4-31 et seq.; license for open recreational events and amusements, § 6-51 et seq.; license for amusement devices in game rooms, § 6-126 et seq.; kennel licenses, § 8-216 et seq.; license for firearm dealers, § 12-91 et seq.; license for hawkers, peddlers and door-to-door salesmen, § 12-161 et seq.; license for junk and secondhand goods dealers, § 12-221 et seq.; license for privately owned camping areas, § 12-286 et seq.; license for taverns, victualing houses, cook shops, etc, § 12-351 et seq.; license for mobile home parks and trailer parks, § 16-151 et seq.; licensed public events and festivals, § 28-46; licensing of solid waste haulers, § 28-41. 

Sec. 12-31. - Renewal or transfer. 
    It shall be a condition for the renewal or transfer of any license (except individual trailer licenses) issued by the town that the holder of the license show that all taxes due to the town by the license holder and by the owner of the premises that are licensed be paid in full. Further, the holder of the license shall present to the town council, prior to the date for renewal or transfer, a statement from the police department approving of the renewal or transfer, a statement from the building and zoning inspector approving of the renewal or transfer and a statement from the appropriate fire company approving of the renewal of transfer. In exercising judgment as to whether to approve or disapprove, the police department, building and zoning inspector and fire company should take into consideration the following: 
(1)  Police department. A background report shall be required. 
(2)  Fire department. The applicant must be in compliance with state fire codes. A signed statement shall be filed by the fire company. 
(3)  Building and zoning inspector. The applicant must comply with G.L. 1956, § 23-27.3-124.0 et seq. (unsafe conditions). The applicant must correct any outstanding zoning violations. 
(4)  Tax collector: The applicant must comply with the town's ordinance regarding payment of taxes for the renewal or transfer of licenses. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1990, § 1; Ord. of 5-8-2003(1), § 1) 
Sec. 12-32. - Denial of renewal. 
    The town council shall not renew any license where the applicant for renewal or transfer shall fail to provide such proof of payment of taxes and the required approvals. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1990, § 2) 
Sec. 12-33. - Application of article provisions. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply in all circumstances except where state or federal law shall otherwise provide in the case of bankruptcies and receiverships. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1990, § 3) 
Secs. 12-34-12-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - FIREARMS DEALERS[3] 
Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference- Discharge of firearms, § 20-3. 
State Law reference- Authority to grant a firearm dealer's license, G.L. 1956, § 11-47-39. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-66. - Authority of article. 
    This article is enacted pursuant to the provisions of G.L. 1956, § 11-47-39 et seq. which provides for firearms dealers' licenses to be issued by cities and towns of this state. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 1) 
Secs. 12-67-12-90. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 12-91. - Required. 
    No person who is not licensed under the provisions of this article shall engage in the business of buying or selling firearms within the town. The term "person," as used in this section, shall mean any individual, firm, corporation, partnership, business or other entity. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 2) 
Sec. 12-92. - Application; contents. 
    Any person applying for a license under this article shall file a written application for such license with the town council. Such applications shall be in a form prescribed by the town clerk and shall include the name of the person applying; the residence and business address of the person applying; a statement as to whether the person applying has ever been arrested or convicted at any time, including misdemeanor and felony arrests and convictions; and any such arrests and convictions shall be listed giving full details of the same. The application shall include the age of the applicant, the applicant's residence addresses for the previous five years and the applicant's social security number. In case the applicant is a corporation, the application shall include the names of all shareholders of the corporation, all directors and all officers. The application shall be subscribed to and sworn to under oath. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 3) 
Sec. 12-93. - Investigation of applicant; report by chief of police; recommendation. 
    Upon receipt of an application under this article, the town clerk shall refer the application to the chief of police who shall make a full investigation of the applicant and shall file a report with the town council with the recommendation of such chief of police as to whether the application should be granted or denied. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 4) 
Sec. 12-94. - Advertisement prior to hearing. 
    Upon receipt of the application with the report of the chief of police, the town council shall cause the application to be advertised in a newspaper of general circulation in the town once a week for three successive weeks prior to the hearing on the license. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 5) 
Sec. 12-95. - Hearing. 
    The town council shall hold a public hearing on the issuance of the license at a time and place to be designated by the council, at which hearing all persons wishing to be heard for or against the issuance of the license shall be given an opportunity to be heard. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 6) 
Sec. 12-96. - Application fee; renewal fee. 
    The application for a license under this article shall be accompanied by an application fee of $75.00. The renewal license fee, as prescribed by G.L. 1956, § 11-47-39 et seq., shall be $5.00. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 7) 
Sec. 12-97. - Federal and state licenses required. 
    No license shall be issued under this article to any person who does not have the requisite federal and state license for dealers in firearms. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 8) 
Sec. 12-98. - Subject to state and federal laws. 
    Any license issued under this article shall be subject to all applicable provisions of federal and state law. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 9) 
Sec. 12-99. - Conditions. 
    Any license issued under this article shall, in addition to other applicable provisions of law, be subject to the following conditions: 
(1)  Location. The business shall be carried on only in the building designated in the license. 
(2)  Display. The license or copy thereof, certified by the issuing authority, shall be displayed on the premises where it can easily be read. 
(3)  Sales of pistols and revolvers. No pistol or revolver shall be sold in violation of any provision of G.L. 1956, § 11-47-1 et seq., nor shall a pistol or revolver be sold under any circumstances unless the purchaser is personally known to the seller or shall present clear evidence of his identity. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 10) 
Sec. 12-100. - Expiration date. 
    Any license issued under this article shall expire on December 31 of each year. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 11) 
Sec. 12-101. - Renewal. 
    Any license issued under this article shall be annually renewable upon payment of an annual renewal fee and a certification of compliance by the license holder with all the terms and conditions of the license. In addition, such annual renewal of such license shall be subject to the ordinance concerning payment of taxes and approval of public safety authorities for the renewal or transfer of licenses issued by the town. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 12) 
Sec. 12-102. - Continuation; annual renewal. 
    All licenses previously issued by the town pursuant to the provisions of G.L. 1956, § 11-47-1 et seq. shall continue in effect, subject to the terms of this article, and shall be renewed annually by the holder pursuant to the terms of this article. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 13) 
Sec. 12-103. - Suspension or revocation; hearing. 
    Any license issued under this article may be suspended or revoked by the town council at any time, for reasonable cause shown, after giving the license holder an opportunity to be heard at a public hearing to be scheduled by the town council. 
(Ord. of 1-4-1990(2), § 14) 
Secs. 12-104-12-135. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - HAWKERS, PEDDLERS AND DOOR-TO-DOOR SALESPERSONS[5] 
Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Cross reference- Streets and sidewalks, ch. 30. 
State Law reference- Hawkers and peddlers, G.L. 1956, § 5-11-1.1 et seq.; local licensing fees, G.L. 1956, § 5-11-2018. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-136. - Authority of article. 
    This article is enacted pursuant to the provisions of G.L. 1956, § 5-11-1.1 et seq. 
(Ord. of 3-8-1990, § 1) 
Sec. 12-137. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Door-to-door salespersons means persons who deliver goods, wares or merchandise to customers for which payment has already been made or is to be made at the time of delivery. Persons selling farm or garden produce, including flowers, and milkmen and persons selling works of art or crafts of their own making at any art or crafts show or exhibition are not deemed to be hawkers, peddlers or door-to-door salespersons. 
    Hawker means any person selling, or offering for sale, any goods, wares or merchandise whatsoever, including any food or beverage, on any public street, highway or public right-of-way in this town from a stationary location. 
    Peddler means any person selling, or offering for sale, any goods, wares or merchandise whatsoever, including any food or beverage, from a vehicle, cart or any other conveyance which is not stationary. 
(Ord. of 3-8-1990, § 2) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 12-138. - Exemptions. 
    Persons selling religious books and publications on behalf of Bible, tract or other religious or moral societies for the purpose of promoting religious or moral improvement, and which are sold for that purpose and not for pecuniary profit, are not deemed to be hawkers, peddlers or door-to-door salespersons. Persons peddling or selling any articles of wearing apparel manufactured with his own hands are not deemed to be hawkers, peddlers or door-to-door salespersons. 
(Ord. of 3-8-1990, § 3) 
Secs. 12-139-12-160. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 12-161. - Duration; expiration date. 
    Licenses issued under this article shall be for the calendar year of issuance and shall expire on December 31 of each year. 
(Ord. of 3-8-1990, § 4) 
Sec. 12-162. - Hearing, notice and fees; issuance preconditions. 
    Licenses shall be issued under this article by the town council after a hearing and public notice given by publication of the application at least one week prior to the date of the hearing. The applicant shall pay, at the time of application, a fee in the amount of $50.00. 
(Ord. of 3-8-1990, § 5) 
Sec. 12-163. - Revocation; notice; hearing. 
    Licenses issued under this article may be revoked for good and just cause. The town council shall give at least one week's notice to the license holder of a hearing on the revocation of the license. Notice shall be given by certified mail to the address given in the license holder's application. Notice shall include a short and concise statement of the alleged good and just cause. After the hearing, the town council may revoke the license upon a finding of good and just cause for revocation. 
(Ord. of 3-8-1990, § 6) 
Sec. 12-164. - Unlicensed sales. 
    No person who is not licensed under this article shall sell or offer for sale any goods, wares or merchandise whatsoever, including food or beverages, as a hawker or peddler within the town. 
(Ord. of 3-8-1990, § 7) 
Secs. 12-165-12-195. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - JUNK AND SECONDHAND GOODS DEALERS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-196. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Automobile junkyard means a place where one or more unserviceable, discarded, wornout or junked automobiles, or bodies, engines, tires, parts or accessories thereof are gathered together. 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 12-197. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person carrying on any of the businesses described in this article without a license shall be punished according to the provisions of section 1-7. 
Secs. 12-198-12-220. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[7] 

Footnotes: 
--- (7) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 12-221. - Required. 
    All persons selling, purchasing, bartering and dealing in junk, old metals and any other secondhand articles and all persons establishing, operating or maintaining automobile junkyards shall be required to obtain a license from the town council. 
Sec. 12-222. - Fees for shopkeepers. 
    The fee for a license for the keeper of a shop or storehouse for the reception of any junk, old metals or secondhand articles which is not an automobile junkyard shall be $25.00. The fee for a license for any foundryman or other person receiving such materials for the purpose of melting the materials or converting such materials into castings shall be $25.00. The fee for a license for the gatherer of such materials in any bag, wagon or cart shall be $25.00. The fee for a license for any person establishing, operating or maintaining an automobile junkyard shall be $25.00. 
Sec. 12-223. - Hearing; notice; posting; filing fees. 
    The town council, before granting a license under this article to keep a shop or storehouse for the reception of any junk, old metals or other secondhand articles or to establish, operate or maintain an automobile junkyard in any location not lawfully occupied for such purpose at the time of the application for such license, shall hold a public hearing notice, which shall be posted at the time of the application for such license; shall hold a public hearing notice which shall be posted at least seven days, but not more than 14 days prior to such hearing in not less than two public places in the town and in a newspaper of general circulation in the town; provided, however, that before the notice of a hearing shall be posted or published, the applicant for the license shall pay a filing fee of $10.00, plus the cost of posting and publishing such notice. 
Sec. 12-224. - Refusal. 
    No license shall be granted under this article to the keeper of any shop or storehouse for the reception of any junk, old metals or other secondhand articles or to the person establishing, operating or maintaining an automobile junkyard in any location not lawfully occupied for such purpose at the time of the application for such purpose at the time of the application for such license where the owners or occupants or the greater part of the land within 200 feet of such building or place shall file with the town council their objection to the granting of such license; provided, however, that this section shall not apply to an applicant who is the keeper of such a shop or storehouse or automobile junkyard within the town which is being acquired under eminent domain proceedings who is applying for a license pursuant to G.L. 1956, § 5-21-1. 
Sec. 12-225. - Conditions for granting for automobile junkyard. 
    No license shall be granted for an automobile junkyard under this article unless: 
(1)  It is to be operated and maintained entirely within a building; 
(2)  It is to be operated and maintained exclusively for the purpose of salvaging the value as scrap of the material collected, as opposed to reselling parts to be used for the purpose for which they were originally manufactured, and is to be located in a built-up commercial or industrial area, or contiguous to a railroad siding, or on or contiguous to docking facilities; or 
(3)  It is: 
a.  More than 600 feet away from any state highway; 
b.  More than 300 feet from any park, bathing beach, playground, school, church or cemetery and is not within ordinary view therefrom; and 
c.  Screened from view either by natural objects or well constructed and properly maintained fences at least six feet high, acceptable to the town council and so specified on the license. 
Sec. 12-226. - Considerations by council. 
    In considering the application for any license under this article, the town council shall consider the character and reputation of the applicants and the nature and location of the proposed site with reference to the character of the surrounding neighborhood and the orderly development of the town. 
Sec. 12-227. - Burning conditions. 
    In granting a license the town council may impose such conditions as it may deem fit with respect to burning. 
Sec. 12-228. - Expiration; revocation. 
    All licenses issued under this article shall expire on December 31 next following the date of issuance and may be revoked at the pleasure of the town council. 
Sec. 12-229. - Limit on number for junkyards. 
    No more than four licenses for automobile junkyards under this article shall be in effect at any one time. 
Sec. 12-230. - Application of section 12-225 to junkyards. 
    The provisions of section 12-225(1), (2) and (3)b shall not apply to any automobile junkyard in existence and having a valid license on the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived. 
Secs. 12-231-12-260. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - PRIVATELY OWNED CAMPING AREAS[8] 
Footnotes: 
--- (8) --- 
Cross reference- Parks and recreation, ch. 22. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-261. - Purpose of article. 
    The purpose of this article is to promote the public health, safety, morals, orderly development and general welfare of the town, and to encourage the development of orderly and well managed camping areas. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § 1) 
Sec. 12-262. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Camping area means any tract or parcel of land set aside for use by persons paying a fee to camp there in tents, similar portable structures and vehicles designed for use in camping, or camping trailers. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § IX) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 12-263. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating each or any of the provisions of this article shall be punished according to the provisions of section 1-7. The town council may also revoke the camping area license as specified in section 12-290. 
(Ord. of 8-22-1991, § I) 
Sec. 12-264. - Operation. 
    Camping areas shall be open and operated during the period from March 1 to December 31 only. 
(Ord. of 8-22-1991, § I) 
Secs. 12-265-12-285. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[9] 

Footnotes: 
--- (9) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 12-286. - Required. 
    No person shall maintain or operate a camping area within the town without a license for such camping area, except as provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § I) 
Sec. 12-287. - Application procedure. 
(a)  Application for a camping area license shall be made in writing to the town council and shall be filed with the town clerk at least four weeks prior to the special or regularly scheduled town council meeting at which hearings on such applications are sought. 
(b)  Such application shall contain the following information: 
(1)  The name and address of the owner of the land on which the camping area is to be established. 
(2)  A description of the facilities intended to be installed on the proposed camping area and the services to be available to persons camping there. 
(c)  Such application shall be accompanied by the following: 
(1)  A plat of the proposed camping area, showing its area and the names and addresses of all property owners adjoining or within 200 feet of the proposed camping areas. 
(2)  Application fee of $50.00 to defray expenses of administering this article. 
(3)  Certificate of the town health officer that the facilities intended to be installed on the proposed camping area and the services to be available to persons camping there will be adequate to meet water supply needs, sewage and garbage disposal needs, and that the proposed camping area will otherwise present a healthy environment for camping. 
(4)  A certificate of the tree warden that the fire prevention facilities intended to be installed on the proposed camping area are adequate, that fire prevention measures intended to be followed at the proposed camping area are adequate and that the proposed camping area will otherwise present a safe environment for camping. 
(d)  The town clerk shall refuse to accept any application not containing the information specified in subsection (b) of this section or not accompanied by the plat, fee and certificates specified in subsection (c) of this section. 
(e)  Upon receipt of a proper application, the town clerk shall send, by regular mail, notice of such application and the date, time and place of the hearing thereon to each of the property owners adjoining or within 200 feet of the proposed location, as shown on the plat accompanying the application. Such notice shall be sent at least three weeks prior to the town council meeting at which such application is to be considered. The town clerk shall also cause the application to be advertised in a newspaper of general circulation in the county, once a week during the two weeks prior to the town council meeting at which such application is to be considered. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § II) 
Sec. 12-288. - Standards governing issuance. 
    No such license shall be granted unless the following standards are met: 
(1)  The proposed camping area must have an area of at least ten acres. 
(2)  No camping facilities or campsites on the proposed camping area shall be located within 200 feet of any adjoining landowner's dwelling house. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § III) 
Sec. 12-289. - Hearing on issuance; issuance or denial. 
    A hearing on the issuance of a camping area license shall be at a special or regularly scheduled town council meeting, after hearing the license shall be granted forthwith if the standards outlined in section 12-288 are met and the proposed location of the camping is found to be compatible with the character and land use of the surrounding neighborhood. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § IV) 
Sec. 12-290. - Conditions required. 
    Any license granted under this article shall be on the following conditions: 
(1)  The license shall not be transferable. 
(2)  The license shall be revocable by the town council for violation of any of the provisions of this article or upon evidence presented by the town health officer or tree warden that the camping area is unhealthy or unsafe, or that adequate health and safety measures are not being followed. 
(3)  The license shall also be revocable by the town council for any violation committed on the premises or of the provisions of any other ordinance or statute, or for maintaining, or allowing the maintenance of, a nuisance on the premises. 
(4)  The license shall permit inspections of the camping area at reasonable times by the town police. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § V) 
Sec. 12-291. - Expiration and renewal; annual fees. 
    All licenses under the authority of this article shall expire on February 1 of each year. Such licenses shall be renewed by payment of an annual license fee of $50.00 to the town treasurer on or before February 1 of each year. 
(Ord. of 6-17-1965, § VI; Ord. of 8-22-1991, § VI) 
Secs. 12-292-12-325. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - TAVERNS, VICTUALING HOUSES, COOKSHOPS, ETC.[10] 
Footnotes: 
--- (10) --- 
Cross reference- Alcoholic beverages, ch. 4. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-326. - Grocery or general stores exempt from article provisions. 
    All persons conducting grocery or general stores are hereby exempt from the provisions of this article. 
Sec. 12-327. - Town clerk to procure suitable licenses and bonds; publication of article. 
    The town clerk is hereby authorized and directed to procure suitable licenses and bonds for the purposes described in this article, and have this article published in conformity with state law. 
Secs. 12-328-12-350. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[11] 

Footnotes: 
--- (11) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 12-351. - Required. 
    No person shall keep a tavern, victualing house, cookshop or oyster house without first having obtained a license therefor from the town clerk. 
Sec. 12-352. - Terms and conditions. 
    Every such license shall specify the person licensed, the business licensed and the building or room in which the business shall be pursued, and shall continue and be in force from December 1 to November 30 following the granting of such license, unless sooner revoked for cause. Every such license shall be given upon such terms and conditions as the town council may from time to time prescribe. 
Sec. 12-353. - Fees. 
    The fee for a tavern, victualing house, cookshop or oyster house license shall be $25.00. The fee for lunch, ice cream, soda and cigar stands, etc., shall be $25.00. 
Sec. 12-354. - Bond-Required for tavern, victualing house, cookshop or oyster house. 
    Every person licensed for the purpose of keeping a tavern, victualing house, cookshop or oyster house, etc., shall give a bond to the town in the sum of $100.00 and shall furnish as surety upon such bond either some person owning real estate within the town or some surety company authorized to do business in the state. Such bond shall be conditioned to comply with the provision of the license and of the law. 
Sec. 12-355. - Same-Required for lunch, ice cream, soda and cigar stand. 
    Every person licensed for the purpose of keeping a lunch, ice cream, soda and cigar stand, etc., shall give a bond to the town in the sum of $50.00, and shall furnish as surety upon such bond either some person owning real estate within the town or some surety authorized to do business in the state. Such bond shall be conditional to comply with the provisions of the license and of the law. 
Sec. 12-356. - Required for keeping billiard table, bagatelle table, pool table or table of similar character. 
    No person shall keep a billiard table, bagatelle table, pool table or any table of similar character in any shop or place of business, or own or keep such table for public use or profit, unless a license for such table shall first be granted by the town council. Such license shall be issued upon such terms and conditions as the town council may from time to time prescribe. 
Sec. 12-357. - License fee in connection with section 12-356. 
    Every person licensed under section 12-356 shall pay to the town treasurer the sum of $50.00. Every such license shall continue and be in force from December 1 to November 30 following the granting of such license, unless sooner revoked for cause. 
Sec. 12-358. - Keeping tables as described in section 12-356 without license; penalty. 
    Every person who shall keep or use any such billiard table, bagatelle table, pool table or any table of similar character without obtaining such license first shall be punished according to the provisions of section 1-7. 
Chapter 14 - LAW ENFORCEMENT[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, ch. 2; officers and employees, § 2-61 et seq.; police access to liquor establishments, § 4-41; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 20; traffic, ch. 36. 
State Law reference- Relief of injured and deceased police officers, G.L. 1956, § 45-19-1 et seq. 

Sec. 14-1. - Purpose of chapter. 
    It is the purpose of this chapter to secure a better regulated and efficient police force to the citizens of the town and to more effectively preserve the peace and good order of the town. 
Sec. 14-2. - Chief of police. 
    The chief of police shall be appointed by the town council and shall serve until his successor is appointed and qualified for office. The chief of police shall serve under the direction and control of the town council and shall be responsible for the administration, control, discipline and good order of the uniformed police force of the town. The chief of police may be removed from office at any time by the town council. 
Cross reference- Officers and employees, § 2-61 et seq. 
Sec. 14-3. - Police officers-Examination; appointment; removal. 
    The chief of police, upon taking office and from time to time thereafter, shall make recommendations to the town council of qualified police constables of the town to serve as uniformed police officers of the town. The town council shall examine the qualifications of each constable so recommended and, if satisfied of his qualifications, shall appoint him a uniformed police officer of the town. Police officers so appointed shall serve under the direction and control of the chief of police. Any police officer may be removed from office at any time by the town council upon a recommendation of the chief of police. 
Sec. 14-4. - Same-Duties. 
    It shall be the duty of every police officer of the town to preserve peace and good order, and to see that all ordinances are promptly enforced. 
Chapter 16 - MANUFACTURED HOMES AND TRAILERS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, ch. 10; businesses, ch. 18; planning, ch. 24; soil erosion and sediment control, ch. 26; solid waste management, ch. 28; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 30; subdivision regulations, ch. 32; zoning, ch. 38; supplementary zoning regulations for house trailers and mobile homes, § 38-280. 
State Law reference- Mobile homes, G.L. 1956, § 31-44-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 16-1-16-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MOBILE HOMES AND HOUSE TRAILERS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 16-31. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Trailer means any portable structure, mobile home, or vehicle designed to be drawn by vehicles or self-propelled and occupied as a dwelling or used for sleeping purposes. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § XV) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 16-32. - Camping trailers in licensed camping areas; trailers in licensed trailer parks. 
    The provisions of this article shall not apply to so-called camping trailers or vehicles designed for use in camping while located in a camping area duly licensed under the town ordinance regulating camping areas (article IV of chapter 12). The provisions of this article shall not apply to trailers located in trailer parks duly licensed under the town ordinance regulating trailer parks (article III of this chapter). 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § XIII; Ord. of 6-17-1965, § I) 
Sec. 16-33. - Penalties; order prohibiting use. 
    Any person violating each or any of the provisions of this article shall be fined $100.00. Each day's violation shall be considered as a separate offense. The town council may also apply to the Superior Court for an order prohibiting the use as a dwelling unit of any trailer located or used in violation of this article. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § XIII) 
Secs. 16-34-16-55. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - INSTALLATION PERMIT 

Sec. 16-56. - Location of trailers without permit prohibited. 
    No person shall locate any trailer for use as a dwelling unit within the town without an installation permit for the same except as provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § I) 
Sec. 16-57. - Procedure for applying for installation permit. 
(a)  Application for an installation permit shall be made in writing to the town council and shall be filed with the town clerk at least four weeks prior to the regularly scheduled town council meeting at which hearing on such application is sought. 
(b)  Such application shall contain the following information: 
(1)  The name and address of the applicant. 
(2)  The name and address of the owner of the trailer. 
(3)  The name and address of the owner of the proposed location of such trailer. 
(4)  A metes and bounds description of the proposed location of such trailer. 
(c)  Such application shall be accompanied by the following: 
(1)  A plat of the proposed location of such trailer prepared by a licensed surveyor showing the area of such location and the names and addresses of all property owners adjoining or within 200 feet of the proposed location. 
(2)  An application fee of $100.00 to defray the expense of administering this article. 
(d)  The town clerk shall refuse to accept any application not containing the information specified in subsection (b) of this section or not accompanied by the plat and fee specified in subsection (c) of this section. 
(e)  Upon receipt of a proper application, the town clerk shall send, by regular mail, notice of such application and the date, time and place of the hearing thereon to each of the property owners adjoining or within 200 feet of the proposed location, as shown on the plat accompanying the application. Such notice shall be sent at least three weeks prior to the town council meeting at which such application is to be considered. The town clerk shall also cause such application to be advertised in a newspaper of general circulation in the county once a week during the two weeks prior to the town council meeting at which such application is to be considered. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § II; Ord. of 7-1-1971, § 1) 
Sec. 16-58. - Standards to govern issuance of installation permit. 
    No such installation permit shall be issued unless the following standards are met: 
(1)  The proposed location shall not be within 1,500 feet of any church, school, library, park, recreation area or municipal building. 
(2)  The proposed location shall have an area of at least 40,000 square feet. 
(3)  The proposed location shall have a frontage on an established public road of at least 175 feet. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § III) 
Sec. 16-59. - Hearing on issuance of installation permit; issuance or denial of permit. 
(a)  Hearings on the issuance of an installation permit shall be held at regularly scheduled town council meetings. After hearing, the installation permit shall be issued forthwith if the standards outlined in section 16-58 are met and the proposed location of the trailer is found to be compatible with the character and land use of the surrounding neighborhood; otherwise, the application shall be denied. 
(b)  Installation permits shall automatically expire six months after they are granted unless a trailer is located on the property and a license granted for the use of said trailer within said six-month period. Installation permits shall not be transferable and any attempt to transfer the same shall result in automatic revocation thereof. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § IV; Ord. of 4-6-1967) 
Sec. 16-60. - Temporary permits. 
    The town council may issue a temporary permit for the location and use of a trailer as a dwelling unit while a dwelling house is under construction at the same location. Such permit shall expire six months after its issue and shall not be extended or renewed. On the expiration of such permit, the trailer must be removed. Such permit shall be issued only after the town council is satisfied that the applicant is acting in good faith and will remove the trailer on the expiration of the temporary permit. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § XII) 
Secs. 16-61-16-80. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - TRAILER LICENSES 

Sec. 16-81. - Unlicensed trailers prohibited. 
    No person shall maintain or use any trailer as a dwelling unit within the town without a license for the same except as provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § V) 
Sec. 16-82. - Procedure for applying for initial trailer license. 
(a)  Application for the initial issuance of a trailer license shall be made in writing to the town council and shall be filed with the town clerk at least two weeks prior to the regularly scheduled town council meeting at which hearing on such application is sought. 
(b)  Such application shall contain a statement that the standards outlined in section 16-83 are met. 
(c)  Such application shall be accompanied by the installation permit previously issued by the town council under section 16-59. 
(d)  The town clerk shall refuse to accept any application not containing the statement specified in subsection (b) of this section or not accompanied by the permit specified in subsection (c) of this section. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § VI) 
Sec. 16-83. - Standards to govern issuance of initial trailer license. 
    No such initial trailer license shall be issued unless the following standards are met: 
(1)  The trailer must be set back at least 30 feet from the road on which it is located and 50 feet from adjoining lot lines. 
(2)  The trailer must have its own individual or municipal water supply and its own septic tank, not used by any other dwelling unit. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § VII) 
Sec. 16-84. - Hearing on issuance of initial trailer license; issuance or denial of license. 
    Hearings on the issuance of an initial trailer license shall be held at regularly scheduled town council meetings. After hearing, the initial trailer license shall be issued forthwith upon payment of the $10.00 annual license fee, if the standards outlined in section 16-83 are met; otherwise, the application shall be denied. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § VIII) 
Sec. 16-85. - Previously located trailers. 
    Trailers located in the town before the effective date of this article must comply with the provisions of any ordinance regulating trailers, including provisions for licensing such trailers, in effect at the time of their location, and must also comply with the provisions of section 16-83(b) (relating to individual water supply and septic tank) and the provisions of section 16-86 (relating to annual license fees). 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § IX) 
Sec. 16-86. - Expiration and renewal of licenses; annual license fees. 
    All licenses issued under the authority of this article or any previous ordinance regulating trailers shall expire on December 31 of each year. Such licenses shall be renewed by payment of an annual license fee of $10.00 to the town treasurer on or before December 31 of each year. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § X) 
Sec. 16-87. - Transfer of licenses. 
    Trailer licenses issued under the authority of this article or any previous ordinance regulating trailers shall not be transferable except upon written application to the town council. The town council shall authorize the transfer of the license if it finds that the location of the trailer is compatible with the character and land use of the surrounding neighborhood at the time the transfer is requested. Any attempt to transfer the license without first obtaining the authorization of the town council shall result in automatic revocation thereof. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(1), § XI) 
Secs. 16-88-16-120. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - MOBILE HOME PARKS AND TRAILER PARKS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference- Businesses, ch. 12. 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 16-121. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Collector means the tax collector of the town. 
    Health officer means the duly appointed health officer of the town or his deputy. 
    Licensee means any person receiving a license to conduct, operate or maintain a mobile home or trailer park or individual mobile home, or trailer, as the case may be. 
    Licensing authority means the town council. 
    Mobile home means a unit or any vehicle used for sleeping or living quarters, permanent or temporary, which is equipped with running water, bath facilities, flush toilet, and appropriate sanitary conditions. 
    Mobile home park or trailer park means privately owned land upon which two or more mobile homes or trailers are or are intended to be used and occupied as sleeping or living quarters, permanent or temporary. 
    Trailer means any house, car, or automobile trailer, other than a mobile home, used for or adaptable for use as living quarters, permanent or temporary. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § I) 
Cross reference- Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 16-122. - General requirements for operation of a mobile home or trailer park. 
(a)  The park shall be located on a site graded to ensure drainage of surface and subsurface water, sewerage, and freedom from stagnant pools. 
(b)  A minimum lot size of 10,000 square feet shall be provided for each mobile home or trailer lot of space. 
(c)  There shall be a minimum of 80 feet clearance between each mobile home or trailer. 
(d)  All mobile home or trailer lots shall abut on a roadway of not less than 30 feet width where off-road parking is provided or 40 feet where no off-road parking is provided. 
(e)  All roads within the park shall be well drained, provided with hard surface, shall be maintained in good condition by the owner or licensee of the mobile home park or trailer park. 
(f)  No mobile home or trailer shall be located closer than 50 feet from the traveled portion of any public highway. 
(g)  Streetlights of not less than 1,000 lumens each shall be installed at intervals of not more than 200 feet apart. 
(h)  The park shall be properly landscaped. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § IV) 
Sec. 16-123. - Sanitary requirements for operation of mobile home or trailer parks. 
(a)  An adequate and potable supply of water with a minimum of 25 pounds per square inch pressure at all times shall be provided for each mobile home or trailer space or lot. The water source shall be capable of producing 300 gallons of potable water per mobile home or trailer lot per day from a source approved by the health officer. 
(b)  No part of the sewerage disposal leaching field system shall be located within 250 feet of any mobile home or trailer park well water supply. 
(c)  Where the sewer lines of a mobile home park or trailer park are not connected to a public sewer, the means of disposal of all sewerage must be approved by the state board of health. 
(d)  Each mobile home or trailer lot shall be provided with an approved electrical connection. 
(e)  Licensees shall furnish at least two refuse cans with tightfitting covers for each occupied mobile home or trailer lot or use any approved collection method in accordance with the state health sanitation laws. Refuse shall be collected and removed regularly and in such manner that no nuisance shall be maintained; it shall be the responsibility of each licensee to maintain proper sanitary conditions with respect to waste and refuse disposal. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § V) 
Cross reference- Solid waste management, ch. 28. 
Sec. 16-124. - Registration of mobile homes or trailers. 
(a)  Each licensee shall keep a register in which the following information shall be recorded forthwith upon the lettering of each mobile home or trailer lot. Such information shall be furnished to the licensing authority by filing same with the town clerk. 
(1)  Full name of mobile home or trailer owner. 
(2)  Make, model, size, serial number, and year of manufacture of mobile home or trailer. 
(3)  State in which registered and registration number, if any. 
(b)  Each licensee shall keep or cause to be kept, for taxation purposes, the following information: 
(1)  The name of the state and the registration or license number of each vehicle; 
(2)  The make, year, length, serial and license number of each mobile home or trailer stationed, maintained, occupied or registered at the mobile home park or trailer park on December 31 of each year. 
Such information shall be filed with the board of tax assessors of the town between January 1 and January 15 in each year. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § VI) 
Sec. 16-125. - Existing land and area requirements. 
    The provisions of sections 16-122 and 16-152, except 16-152(a) and (d) shall not apply to any mobile home or trailer site located within the town prior to the effective date of the ordinance from which this article derives. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § X) 
Sec. 16-126. - Penalties for violation. 
    Any person who shall violate any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be fined not more than $25.00 for each offense. Each day a violation shall continue shall be deemed a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § VIII) 
Secs. 16-127-16-150. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Cross reference- Business licenses, § 12-31 et seq. 

Sec. 16-151. - Required. 
    No person shall maintain or operate a mobile home park or trailer park without having first obtained a license from the licensing authority. These regulations shall apply forthwith to all existing mobile home or trailer parks; provided, however, that the licensing authority shall, upon application, grant such extension of time or waive such requirements (other than sanitary requirements) as may in its judgment be required by the specific circumstances. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § II) 
Sec. 16-152. - Application. 
(a)  An application for a mobile home park or trailer park license shall contain the following: 
(1)  Name and address of the applicant, and name and address of real party in interest if other than the applicant. 
(2)  A plot plan made by a licensed surveyor under seal showing the site of the mobile home park or trailer park, roads, location, size, shape and identification number of the mobile home or trailer lots or spaces, locations of sanitary provisions and the name of abutting property owners according to the records of the board of tax assessors. 
(3)  Certificate of approval of the health officer as to compliance with the sanitary requirements set forth. 
(4)  The initial fee for a permit for a mobile home park or trailer park shall be $125.00 payable to the town clerk. Any renewal of such permit thereafter shall be $125.00 per year. 
(5)  Proof of ownership, option or valid lease of the premises to be used as a mobile home park or trailer park. 
(6)  Approval of the planning board. 
(b)  No original license for a mobile home or trailer park shall be granted or issued until a public hearing advertised at least once a week for three successive weeks in a public newspaper published in the county shall be held by the licensing authority. 
(Ord. of 5-6-1965(2), § III) 
Chapter 18 - NUISANCES[1] 
Footnotes:

ARTICLE II. - NOISE 

Sec. 18-31. - Creation of certain sounds declared nuisance. 
    It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and it shall be unlawful for any person to make, cause or suffer, or permit to be made or caused upon any premises owned, occupied or controlled by him, or upon any public property, public roadway or thoroughfare in the town, unnecessary noise or sounds by means of the human voice, or, by any other means or methods which are physically annoying to persons, or which are so harsh, or so prolonged or unnatural, or, unusual in their use, time and place as to occasion physical discomfort or which are injurious to the lives, health, peace and comfort of the inhabitants of the town. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1982, § I) 
Sec. 18-32. - Penalty for violation of article. 
    Any person violating this article shall be fined an amount not exceeding $100.00. 
(Ord. of 2-4-1982, § II) 
Chapter 20 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Law enforcement, ch. 14. 
State Law reference- Offenses punishable by state law not to be imposed by ordinance, G.L. 1956, § 45-6-6; criminal offenses, G.L. 1956, § 11-1-1 et seq. 

Sec. 20-1. - Disorderly conduct; penalty for violation of section. 
    Every person who shall revel, commit any nuisance or mischief, disturb the peace, quarrel or otherwise behave in an indecent or disorderly manner in any public building, public hall, public place of amusement, church, public school, street, highway, public bridge, public lands, burial grounds, public parks, or any public place in the town of any establishment or club which serves or caters to the public, to the disturbance or annoyance of the peaceable inhabitants of the town, or any portion of them, or shall assist, aid, encourage or promote the same to be done by any other person shall be fined for each offense the sum of $20.00, or imprisoned for a term not to exceed ten days. 
State Law reference- Disorderly conduct, G.L. 1956, § 11-45-1. 
Sec. 20-2. - Indecent intoxication. 
    Any person who shall be found intoxicated under such circumstances as to amount to a violation of decency in any highway, street, gangway or other public place in this town shall, upon conviction, be fined for each and every offense not less than $5.00 nor more than $20.00, or be imprisoned not more than ten days. 
Cross reference- Alcoholic beverages, ch. 4. 
State Law reference- Authority to adopt an ordinance to punish indecent intoxication, G.L. 1956, § 45-6-3. 
Sec. 20-3. - Discharge of firearms; penalty for violation of section. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any firearms within a distance of 500 feet from any building within the town; provided, however, that this section shall not apply to the owner or lessee of any such building, or to the immediate members of his family. 
(b)  Any person who shall violate the provisions of this section shall, upon conviction, be fined not exceeding $20.00 or imprisoned not exceeding ten days for each such violation. 
Cross reference- Firearms dealers, § 12-66 et seq. 
State Law reference- Weapons, G.L. 1956, § 11-47-1 et seq. 
Chapter 22 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) ---
